Title: Breakdown of the Migdal-Eliashberg theory for electron-phonon systems. Role of polarons/bi-polarons

URL Source: https://arxiv.org/pdf/2604.14294v2

Published Time: Wed, 22 Apr 2026 00:15:07 GMT

Number of Pages: 64

Markdown Content:
# Breakdown of the Migdal-Eliashberg theory for electron-phonon systems. Role of polarons/bi-polarons 

Andrey Chubukov, 1 Ilya Esterlis, 2 Artem Abanov, 3 and Nikolay Prokof‚Äôev 4

> 1

Department of Physics, University of Minnesota, Minneapolis, MN 55455, USA 

> 2

Department of Physics, University of Wisconsin-Madison, Madison, WI 53706-1390, USA 

> 3

Department of Physics, Texas A&M University, College Station, TX 77843, USA USA 

> 4

Department of Physics, University of Massachusetts, Amherst, MA 01003, USA 

The Migdal-Eliashberg theory (MET) describes electrons interacting with phonons in the adia-batic limit when the phonon Debye frequency is much smaller than the Fermi energy. A conventional belief is that MET holds even at strong coupling, when electron self-energy is large, and breaks down only near the point where the dressed phonon spectrum softens to near zero. We analyze numeri-cally and analytically a different option‚ÄĒcollapse to a polaronic/bipolaronic ground state. The last scenario has never been analyzed in precise quantitative terms for a generic electron density. Using variational considerations, we establish rigorous upper bounds on the coupling őĽ, at which a FL state transforms into the bipolaron/polaron state. We show that at small and near-maximum densi-ties, this happens well before a dressed phonon softens. This is true both in 2D and 3D systems; in the latter the upper bound on őĽ tends to zero in the limit of small or near-full density. We present analytical reasoning for this behavior based on hints extracted from exact diagrammatic treatment of the on-site Holstein model for the spin polarized case and argue that polarons are produced by fermions with energies comparable to the bandwidth; i.e., polaron formation is outside the realm of MET. Closer to half-filling, the leading instability upon increasing őĽ is towards a charge-density-wave state (CDW), and there exists a strong coupling regime of MET near this instability, while the polaron/bipolaron state develops at larger őĽ out of a CDW-ordered state and inherits a CDW order over some range of coupling.

> I. INTRODUCTION

An incredibly rich and fascinating physics displayed by a system of fermions interacting with lattice vibra-tions (phonons) continues to attract significant interest among researchers interested in various aspects of strong correlations and superconductivity (see, e.g. the review articles [1‚Äď4]). Models of coupled electron-phonon (e-ph) systems, particularly the one of fermions interact-ing with a single Einstein phonon, have long been con-sidered as the best examples of applicability of Migdal-Eliashberg theory (MET), both in the normal and su-perconducting state; see, e.g., Refs. [5‚Äď7]. At weak cou-pling, MET is synonymous to perturbation theory/BCS theory of superconductivity with the advantage that no artificial high-energy cutoff is required, e.g., supercon-ducting Tc can be computed exactly, including the pref-actor [8‚Äď11] [12]. At strong coupling, MET states that in the adiabatic limit, when the Debye frequency, ŌČ0, is much smaller than the Fermi energy, EF , one can proceed beyond the perturbation theory and rigorously analyze properties of both normal and superconducting states, despite a large enhancement of the fermionic mass and a non-FL behavior in a wide range of frequencies. Specif-ically, MET states that at strong coupling, one can still use a self-consistent one-loop approximation because ver-tex corrections remain small in ő≥ = ŌČ0/E F ‚Č™ 1. The physical argument is that in the scattering processes, ac-counting for vertex corrections, fermions with typical mo-menta of the order kF vibrate at frequencies comparable to ŌČ0, far away from their own resonance at EF .More recent studies, which intensified over the last few years with the advent of more powerful analyti-cal and numerical methods, questioned the existence of the strong-coupling regime described by MET. One ar-gument here is technical - in many cases the effective Debye frequency dressed by interaction with fermions acquires rather strong momentum dependence, which qualitatively changes the structure of the one-loop self-consistent theory and the rational for neglecting vertex corrections. Another argument, outlined in Ref. [13], points to a possibility that in the strong coupling regime the MET theory undergoes a kinetic instability at which the phonon and electron subsystems develop a tempera-ture difference. And the most drastic argument is that even before the system enters a strong coupling regime, it may undergo a radical reconstruction of low-energy exci-tations due to emergence of polarons and bi-polarons as relevant degrees of freedom [14, 15]. In this communication, we analyze the interplay be-tween MET and polaron/bipolaron formation at T = 0 for several systems (in two- and three-dimensions) with e-ph interaction, including interaction with an Einstein phonon with frequency ŌČ0. We combine a variational numerical analysis and an analytical (diagrammatic) ap-proach and analyze the evolution of the system‚Äôs behavior with increasing e-ph coupling at various fermionic filling factors n. We keep the ratio of the e-ph interaction and the Debye frequency fixed at a large value and vary the bandwidth W . We analyze how the fermionic density of state (DOS) evolves as W decreases and eventually van-ishes. We introduce fermions that behave as free quasi-particles in the limit W ‚Üí ‚ąě and express the DOS of the FL, described by MET, and of a polaron state in terms of the same fermions. In other words, we do not intro-duce new fermionic operators for electron-phonon bound states, as is often done in the analysis of a polaron state (see, e.g., [16]). For an Einstein phonon with frequency ŌČ0, the limit 

W = 0 is described by the exactly solvable Holstein model. In the latter, the DOS of spin-less (spin-polarized) fermions consists of a set of őī-functional peaks separated by ŌČ0 (Fig. 1b). These peaks correspond to po-larons, which can be interpreted as ‚Äúbound states‚ÄĚ of an electron and strong lattice deformation (see more on this interpretation below). The peak with the smallest energy is the ground state, whereas other peaks are states fea-turing multiple excited phonons relative to the ground state. For spin-full fermions, phonon-mediated pairing interaction between polarons made of fermions with op-posite spins binds polarons into bi-polarons. This leads to vanishing of the DOS around ŌČ = 0. For both polarons and bi-polarons, the DOS is quite different from that at small e-ph coupling őĽ, which is continuous at ŌČ = 0 and has a width W (Fig. 1a). Using numerical and analytical studies, we present the theoretical scenario for the evolution of the system at different W and fermionic density n (see Figs. 2 and 3). In the numerical study, we consider S = 1 /2 fermions, for which the polaron state is that of heavy bi-polarons (bound states of two electrons dressed by lattice distor-tion). We compare ground state energies and chemical potentials of the FL (FL) state, described by MET, and the variational state consisting of localized bi-polarons, identify the ranges of couplings at which either the pure bi-polaron state or the mixed state with bi-polaron and FL components is energetically favorable, and compare this coupling with the one at which the dressed phonon spectrum softens to zero. In the analytical study, we consider spin-less fermions (a spin-polarized system), in which case there are po-larons but no bi-polarons. We first develop a diagram-3

We also analyze how a polaron state emerges if one departs from the FL and increases the coupling. In both numerical and analytical study we consider a particle-hole symmetric model for which the behavior at small fermionic densities is the same as near the full filling. For spinful fermions, the phase diagram is sym-metric with respect to n = 1; for spin-less fermions, it is symmetric around n = 1 /2.  

> A. Notations and summary of the results

For convenience of the reader, we present below the list of notation and a short summary of the results of our numerical and analytical studies, focusing on n ‚Č§ 1 for spin-full fermions and n ‚Č§ 1/2 for spin-less fermions.

> 2. Numerical results

We considered S = 1 /2 fermions with a tight-binding dispersion relation on the simple cubic lattice in three dimensions (3D) and the square lattice in 2D. We in-troduced a local density-displacement-type coupling to lattice vibrations and probed several typical phonon dis-persions. For the FL state, we compute the critical value 

őĽc, 20 for an electronic CDW instability, obtain the mo-menta at which the instability takes place, and evalu-ate the dressed coupling őĽr . We then compared the en-ergy and chemical potential of the FL state at various fermionic densities with those of the variational bipolaron (BP) state composed of localized fermion pairs. For the cases where the bottom of the dispersion of bare phonons is close to q = 0, we considered a homogeneous state with the highest density ni = 2 at N n/ 2 sites ( N is the to-tal number of sites). For the cases where the bottom 4

The phase diagram obtained in variational (left) and analytical (right) analysis for a homogeneous polaron order on the ( őĽp, n ) plane, where őĽpis the ratio of polaron binding energy and fermionic bandwidth and nis the density of fermions. The variational phase diagram has been obtained for spin-full electrons and bi-polarons. It is adjusted here to spinless fermions and polarons for comparison with the analytical phase diagram. We see that the two phase diagrams are identical. We explain in the text why this is so. The phase diagram contains the regions of a Fermi liquid (FL), described by MET, a homogeneous polaron state, a charge-ordered state of electrons (CDW) and mixed states, in which both polaron and electronic components are present. for the transformation of the FL state into the mixed FL + bi-polaron state (which is likely to be phase sepa-rated) by analyzing the coupling at which the chemical potentials of the FL and BP states become equal. We emphasize that once bi-polarons appear, the description based on MET becomes invalid, although the theory it-self remains internally stable against low-energy fluctu-ations. We then identified the larger critical coupling, corresponding to the upper end of the mixed state, as the one at which the chemical potential of the BP state reaches the bottom of the electron dispersion. At even larger coupling, the ground state is a BP state with lo-calized fermionic pairs. We show the results in Figs. 4 and 5 in units of őĽ0 and re-express some of these results in units of őĽp in Figs. 2 and 31. In 3D (Fig. 4), we found that in the low den-sity limit őĽc, 10 is proportional to the Fermi momentum, i.e. it scales as n1/3, while őĽc, 20 = O(1) ( őĽc, 20 = 1 /2for fermions with a parabolic dispersion). In this situa-tion, bi-polarons appear, and the description within the MET becomes invalid already at weak coupling, when the MET is well inside its stability region. In other words, the low-density (continuous) limit of the MET in 3D is ill-defined. As density increases, őĽc, 10 also increases, while 

őĽc, 20 decreases. We showed that for some phonon disper-sions, there exists a range of fermion densities around half-filling nc < n < 1 where őĽc, 20 < őĽ c, 10 . In this range, the internal instability of the MET towards a CDW order develops before the polaron formation. We also analyzed the structure of the mixed state in this range and found the line at which the FL component in the mixed state loses a CDW order as the frequency increases őĽ0. This line can be viewed as an extension of the őĽc, 20 line to the mixed state. We found that őĽc, 20 (n)displays a re-entrant behavior at n > n c.As őĽ approaches őĽc, 20 from below, the system should nominally go into the strong coupling regime of MET, where the dressed őĽr becomes large. However, we found that in most cases that we studied, őĽr remains O(1) even in the vicinity of őĽc, 20 . We associate this with the fact that for finite n, the phonon spectrum softens only at isolated momentum points, and the phase space around the softening is not large enough to bring the system into the strong coupling regime in a detectable range of

> 3. Analytical results

We considered 2D spinless fermions with tight-binding dispersion coupled to a dispersion-less phonon with fre-quency ŌČ0. We obtained three sets of analytical results: one for an infinitesimally small density n = 0+, an-other for an infinitesimally small deviation for full fill-ing n = 1 ‚ąí, and the third for arbitrary n. We present the analytical phase diagrams for the homogeneous and checkerboard polaron configurations in the right panel in Fig. 2 and in Fig. 27, respectively. For cases n = 0 and n = 1, we first demonstrate that the exact DOS of the Holstein model in the limit W = 0 is reproduced using the eikonal diagrammatic approach. We then ex-tend the diagrammatic analysis to finite W and argue that the DOS can be approximated by a set of narrow, nearly őī‚ąífunctional peaks at low energies, ŌČ = mŌČ 0,

m = 0 , 1, 2, etc. for n = 0 and m = 0 , ‚ąí1, ‚ąí2 for n = 1, which describe heavy polarons with exponentially large mass eő≤ and a free-particle-like continua of width W , cen-tered at much larger ŌČ = ő≤ŌČ 0 at n = 0 and at ŌČ = ‚ąíő≤ŌČ 0

at n = 1. As W increases, the lower end of the con-tinuum moves towards ŌČ = 0, absorbing low-energy po-larons one by one. The last polaron at ŌČ = 0 is absorbed at őĽc, 1 

> p

= 1 /2. At smaller őĽp, the system is in a FL state described by MET. There is no mixed state for n = 0 and n = 1. For these n, we found őĽc, 2

= ŌÄ/ 4, which is larger than őĽc, 1

= 1 /2 from smaller őĽp and argued that the onset of the polaron instability is the development of a peak in the DOS at the lower end of the continuum, which can be interpreted as a polaron bound state. We argued that the bound state is not a low-energy phenomenon de-spite that it appears at ŌČ equal to the chemical potential, because the corresponding contribution to the fermionic self-energy comes from high-order, O(ő≤), in the diagram-matic series and involves fermions with energies compa-rable to W . Fluctuations of these high-energy fermions are disconnected from fluctuations of low-energy fermions with energies well within W , which determine the stabil-ity of MET. At a finite n, we found that one has to do a calculation in three steps to reproduce the exact DOS of the Holstein model at W = 0. First, one has to add an ancilla fermion ňúc ‚Äď a hole-like excitation with the opposite value of the chemical potential compared to őľn = (2 n ‚ąí 1) ő≤ŌČ 0 for the original electron c (for each, őľn is the chemical poten-tial without the Hartree contribution, the total chemical potential őľP = ‚ąíő≤ŌČ 0) Second, one has to introduce a condensate order parameter ‚ąÜ = < c ‚Ä†c > and use it to de-couple the phonon-induced interaction between the den-sities of the original and ancilla fermions. We obtained a non-zero value of ‚ąÜ from the minimization of the ground state energy and verified that the energy is smaller at a finite ‚ąÜ = 2 ő≤0(n(1 ‚ąí n)1/2. Diagonalizing the effective quadratic Hamiltonian we found two sets of fermions with energies ¬Īő≤ŌČ 0, which can be identified as describing the filled and empty states. The electron-phonon interaction decouples between these new fermions, and the effective Hamiltonian becomes the sum of the two terms: one is the same as for n = 0, and the other is the same as for 

n = 1. Third, one has to do eikonal calculations for n = 0 and n = 1 components. Using this procedure, we repro-duced the exact DOS for the physical fermion consisting of two sets of őī-functions at ŌČ ‚Č• 0 and ŌČ ‚Č§ 0, the first with the overall factor 1 ‚ąí n and the second with the overall factor n.We then extended the calculations at 0 < n < 1/2 to fi-nite W . Now the condensate order parameter ‚ąÜ has to be selected with a particular momentum q, We analyzed two polaron states: a homogeneous one with ‚ąÜ q=0 = ‚ąÜ 0 and a checkerborad one with ‚ąÜ q=Q = ‚ąÜ Q, where Q = ( ŌÄ, ŌÄ ). 6We verified that the ‚ąÜ 0 state is localized with no density fluctuations between occupied and non-occupied states, We showed that the DOS of each polaron state can be approximated by a set of narrow, nearly őī‚ąífunctional peaks at low energies, ŌČ = nŌČ 0, n = 0 , ¬Ī1, ¬Ī2, etc., which describe heavy polarons with exponentially large mass eő≤ and two free continua at higher energies, cen-tered at ŌČ = ¬Īő≤ŌČ 0, each with width W . As W increases and őĽp decreases, the lower edges of the two continua ex-tend to smaller |ŌČ| and absorb low-energy polarons one by one. For the homogeneous polaron state, the edges of the two continua merge at ŌČ = 0 at őĽp = 1 /2. We found that at smaller őĽp, the ground state is a mixed state, in which a portion of a system with density n ‚ąí őī is in the homogeneous polaron state and the other portion, with density őī is in a FL state. Finally, we combined the phase diagrams in Figs. 2and 27 and obtained the complete phase diagram, Fig. 3, assuming that the homogeneous polaron state develops in smaller n and the checkerboard polaron state devel-ops near n = 1 /2. Exactly at half-filling, we found a degeneracy between ( ŌÄ, ŌÄ ) polaron and ( ŌÄ, ŌÄ ) electronic orders and argued that this leads to an enhanced order parameter manifold.  

> 4. The structure of the paper

The structure of the paper is the following. In Sec. II we introduce the model, set up the notation, and briefly review MET. In Section III we examine the physics of spin-1 /2 fermions numerically using the variational ap-proach. In Section IV we present our analytical results for spin-less fermions. We first consider the limiting cases of zero and filled band densities and then present re-sults for arbitrary n. We compare our analytical and numerical results in Sec. V in 2D and 3D and discuss a comparison with previous numerical studies of the sys-tem evolution with increasing coupling. We present our conclusions in Sec.VI. Some technical details are pre-sented in the Appendices. In particular, in Appendix C we rationalize the need to include vertex corrections into diagrammatic treatment by comparing the eikonal tech-nique, which treats self-energy and vertex corrections on equal footing and reproduces the exact result for the Hol-stein model, with rainbow and self-consistent one-loop approximations, both of which neglect vertex corrections.   

> II. THEORETICAL SETUP AND MET A. Theoretical setup

We consider a lattice model of fermionic density cou-pled to lattice vibrations. In its simplest form, the cou-pling is between the electron density and a single phonon mode. The corresponding interaction Hamiltonian is (in notation closely following the textbook [7])

> B. Migdal-Eliashberg theory

controls the strength of vertex corrections and the Landau damp-ing term in the bosonic propagator. Sometimes, the effec-tive fermion-phonon coupling with dimension of energy is defined as u2 = NF g2 (see, e.g., [18, 19]. In these nota-tions, őĽ0 = u2/ŌČ 20 and őĽE 

> 0

‚ąľ u2/(EF ŌČ0). We emphasize that of four parameters, only three - g, ŌČ0 and EF - ap-pear in MET. The bandwidth scale W does not appear there as MET assumes that there are no interesting ef-fects coming from fermions with energies comparable to 

W . Moreover, the scale EF is important only in the adi-abatic condition that sets the validity of MET. The distinction between MET and conventional per-turbation theory follows from the argument [5, 6] that MET remains under control even outside the applicabil-ity of a perturbative expansion when the renormalized dimensionless coupling őĽr , Eq. (4), becomes larger than one. This holds as long as the Eliashberg parameter remains small and vertex corrections can be neglected. From a mathematical perspective, MET in the strong coupling regime is a self-consistent one-loop theory. It was understood early on [5‚Äď7] that the applicability con-dition of MET must be formulated not in terms of the bare couplings ( őĽ0, őĽ E 

> 0

) but in terms of the renormalized ones ( őĽr , őĽ Er ), based on the phonon spectrum softened by electron polarization. In the adiabatic regime, the dynamic renormalization of the phonon propagator due to Landau damping is small and can be neglected for the same reason as vertex corrections, while the renormal-ization by the real part of the static polarization changes 

ŌČ0(q) to dressed ŌČr (q). Accordingly, the renormalized e-ph couplings in MET theory are defined by

For a generic dispersion, ŌČr (q) soft-ens to zero at q = qc at some őĽ0 = őĽc ‚ąľ O(1). Thus, MET cannot be extended beyond this őĽc. However, it has been argued that a controlled MET may still hold at őĽ0 ‚Č§ őĽc provided renormalized couplings obey the in-equality őĽEr ‚Č™ 1, i.e. there still exists a range of őĽ0 where 

őĽr > 1 but őĽEr ‚Č™ 1. The situation is somewhat special for an Einstein phonon and parabolic fermionic dispersion in 2D. Here, the free-fermion polarization operator at T = 0 does not depend on q for |q| < 2kF , i.e., for any momentum trans-fer between fermions on the Fermi surface. As a result, 

ŌČr = ŌČ0(1 ‚ąí 2őĽ0)1/2 remains momentum independent, leading to őĽr = őĽ0/(1 ‚ąí 2őĽ0) and őĽEr = őĽE 

> 0

/(1 ‚ąí 2őĽ0)1/2,8with a stronger divergence of őĽr as őĽ0,c ‚Üí 1/2. The self-energy in this case is given by ő£( ŌČm) = ‚ąíiőĽ r ŌČr arctan ŌČm

ŌČr

. (10) At small ŌČm, ő£( ŌČm) = ‚ąíiőĽ r ŌČm. The strong coupling condition őĽr ‚Čę 1, őĽEr ‚Č™ 1 is satisfied at 1 ‚Čę 1 ‚ąí 2őĽ0 ‚Čę

ŌČ20 /(2 EF )2. Within this regime (if it holds) the mass renormalization is strong but vertex corrections are still small. However, even in this regime, the self-energy is relevant only for fermions with frequencies ŌČm < E F őĽEr ,which remain smaller than EF as long as the dressed Eliashberg parameter őĽEr remains small. In our analysis, we explore the relevance of the third dimensionless parameter, EF /W . It is of order one at densities around half-filling, but is small at low fermionic density n. We show that at small EF /W , the polaron state wins energetically over the FL state already at small 

őĽ0 (parametrically small in 3D and numerically small in 2D), i.e. the development of a polaron state is not re-lated to the softening of the phonon spectrum. We fur-ther argue that polaron formation is not a low-energy phenomenon. Rather, it involves electronic states with energies exceeding the bandwidth, i.e. when the conduc-tion band is nearly empty, the FL state becomes unstable because of fluctuations outside the low-frequency range considered in MET. To put it differently, fermions with energies comparable to the bandwidth rather than the ones near the Fermi surface control which state is the true vacuum (by particle-hole symmetry, the same holds in the opposite limit of nearly completely occupied band, when W ‚ąí EF << W ). For fermionic densities around half-filling, the lead-ing instability upon increasing őĽ0 is phonon softening at some qc, while a polaron state develops at a larger coupling.  

> III. NUMERICAL ANALYSIS

We considered several systems with electron-phonon interaction (1) in cubic and square lattices to determine the critical values of őĽ0 and őĽr as functions of the electron density, n, or EF /W ratio. We increased the coupling and checked at which őĽ0 (i) the energy of a localized BP state becomes smaller than that of the FL, (ii) the chem-ical potential of the BP state becomes lower than that of a FL, and (iii) the dressed phonon spectrum softens to zero at some momentum. When the bottom of the bare phonon dispersion is near q = Q = ( ŌÄ, ŌÄ, ŌÄ ), we considered the state with a checkerboard arrangement of sites with localized pairs, which in this case has a lower energy EbBP than a ho-mogeneous state. In the localized BP-CDW state, if a given site has a bi-polaron, then the neighboring site is empty and the next-nearest one again has a bi-polaron. For the checkerboard arrangement of the n < 1, Ne ‚Č§ N

sites, other sites are just empty (for the n > 1, 2 N ‚ąí Ne

> BP

/N e.This treatment is used throughout the manuscript with the exception of subsection IV D 3) where we consider the checkerboard polaron order near half-filling. We show the results in Fig. 4 for a 3D system and in Fig. 5 for a 2D system. In the left panels of both fig-ures, we show the bare and renormalized phonon spectra at the critical density/coupling when the spectrum first touches zero at some momentum qc for three types of a bare phonon dispersion, i.e. the plots are for a particular density n = nc or n = nc, 1 marked in the middle panels. In the middle panels, we show the phase diagrams in the (őĽ0, n ) plane for 0 < n < 1. We considered a variational homogeneous BP state for the cases when the bare phonon spectrum has a minimum at momentum q = 0 (the upper and lower rows) and a variational checkerboard BP state for the cases when the renormalized phonon spectrum has a minimum at momentum Q (the middle rows in both figures). In the right panels, we show the renormalized coupling őĽr for couplings at which the mixed state emerges before the phonon spectrum softens. There are two key critical lines in the phase diagrams: 

őĽc, 10 , at which bi-polarons emerge, and őĽc, 20 , at which the phonon spectrum softens at qc. At densities n < n c (or 

n < n c, 1 and n > n c, 2) we have őĽc, 10 < őĽ c, 20 , i.e. a pure FL state becomes unstable towards bi-polarons, while MET is still internally stable. For a 3D system, we found that 

őĽc, 10 is smaller than 0 .5 for all three types of bare phonon dispersion in Fig. 4. Furthermore, at small densities, cor-responding to a near-spherical Fermi surface, őĽc, 10 tends to zero as n1/3 due to vanishing NF ‚ąľ pF ‚ąľ n1/3 while a putative őĽc, 20 remains finite. As a result, at n ‚Üí 0, a FL becomes unstable against bi-polarons already at infinitesimally small őĽ0. This contradicts earlier claims that in the continuous limit, corresponding to small n,an electron-phonon system is well described by the MET because the dressed őĽr is also small as n1/3.In 2D, őĽc, 10 tends to a finite value 1 /ŌÄ at n ‚Üí 0 (see Fig. 5) because in this limit NF does not depend on the Fermi momentum. Still, we found that this value is smaller than the putative őĽc, 20 at n ‚Üí 0, i.e., at small n

a FL again becomes unstable against bi-polarons before the phonon spectrum softens. In actual calculations, we identified őĽc, 10 as the line at which the chemical potentials of a FL and a variational BP state become equal, őľBP = őľF L . We explicitly ver-ified that a further increase of őĽ0 leads to a mixed (or phase separated) state consisting of heavy bi-polarons at density nbi , which increases in volume with increasing 

őĽ0, and FL fermions at density n ‚ąí 2nbi , which decreases 12 with increasing őĽ0. The same holds if we increase n keep-ing őĽ0 fixed at a value above őĽc, 10 and increase n: extra electrons form bi-polarons, while the number of itinerant electrons remains intact. The chemical potentials őľBP 

and őľF L remain equal within the mixed phase, as re-quired by the Maxwell construction. The mixed phases (with or without CDW order in its components) are lo-cated in the middle panels between őĽc, 10 and the upper solid black line, at which 2 nbi = n. At larger őĽ0, the entire system consists of bi-polarons. In 2D, the upper boundary of the mixed state diverges at half-filling as for the tight-binding dispersion the 2D DOS diverges at 

n = 1. At densities n > n c (or nc, 1 < n < n c, 2), we have 

őĽc, 20 < őĽ c, 10 . In this situation, the system first develops an electronic CDW order at őĽc, 20 , and the mixed state emerges at őĽc, 10 out of a CDW state. We found in our variational analysis that for these n, there exists another line inside the mixed state (solid red lines in the middle sections of Figs. 4 and 5) at which the order of CDW electrons disappears as the number of őĽ0. For a 3D sys-tem with a dispersion-less bare phonon, the range of őĽ0,in which a FL component of the mixed phase is CDW-ordered, is tiny (the lower middle panel in Fig. 4), but for other bare dispersions in 3D and for all bare disper-sions in 2D it is sizable. We also note that a large value of nc ‚Č§ 1 in the upper middle panel of Fig. 5 is the consequence of our choice of a bare 2D dispersion with a minimum at q = 0. For a more flat bare dispersion, nc

is far from half-filling (see the lower middle panel in Fig. 5). For the checkerboard bi-polaron state, variational anal-ysis yields two critical nc1 and nc2 both in 3D and in 2D (the central middle panels in Figs. 4 and 5). In 3D the onset coupling for the instability towards the BP-CDW state vanishes not only at n = 0 but also at half-filling, due to extra potential energy gained by the checkerboard arrangement of bi-polarons. In this situa-tion, CDW instability of itinerant fermions occurs prior to the formation of bi-polarons only in a slice of densi-ties nc1 < n < n c2. The range of couplings where the system displays a pure CDW order is also very narrow. This is arguably one of the most surprising results of our variational analysis. Next, it is generally expected that near the onset of a CDW instability, a Fermi-liquid enters a strong-coupling regime where the dressed őĽr ‚Čę 1 (Refs. [22, 23], or be-comes unstable by some other mechanism [13]. However, because phonon softens only at discrete points in momen-tum space and the dressed coupling, őĽr ‚ąĚ ‚ü® ŌČ‚ąí2 

> r

(q)‚ü©F S ,involves averaging over q connecting points on the Fermi surface, the increase of őĽr near the instability is far less drastic [9, 24] than in the special case when ŌČr is treated as momentum independent and softens simultaneously at all momenta (see [19] and references therein). The dimensionality of space matters here: the corresponding momentum integral over the Fermi surface is more singu-lar in 2D. For ŌČ2 

> r

(q ‚Üí qc) ‚Üí őī2 + c(q ‚ąí qc)2 with őī ‚Č™ ő©, we have őĽr ‚ąĚ | ln[ őī]| in a 3D system and őĽr ‚ąĚ 1/őī in 2D. Thus, despite the dramatic softening of ŌČr at some momentum, the increase of őĽr is quite moderate, except for the very close vicinity of a CDW transition, which is difficult to reach numerically. We did simulations with 

N = 256 3 sites for 3D systems with various bare phonon spectra and found that őĽr barely exceeds unity at n = nc,see the right panels in Fig. 4. We found similar results in the 2D system with N = 1024 2 sites (right panels in Fig. 5). Moreover, in real materials, a structural transi-tion is often weakly first-order, i.e., őī is reduced near the transition but does not vanish. Equation (6) also makes it clear that neglecting the momentum dependence of ŌČr is highly unphysical be-cause it implies that the bare phonon spectrum has to be adjusted to compensate for the momentum dependence of ŌČr coming from a particle-hole polarization bubble. Finally, we emphasize that our variational analysis es-tablishes the upper bounds on őĽc, 1 as we only analyzed two variational states with localized bi-polarons. Other potential variational bi-polaron states include extended bound states of pairs or electron delocalization in a homo-geneous bi-polaron state. Also, even if the polaron order emerges with zero or near-zero momentum at n = nc,it may evolve as n approaches half-filling. This is par-ticularly true in 2D as the very near half-filling of the polarization bubble at Q = ( ŌÄ, ŌÄ ) is logarithmically sin-gular, hence the polaron state is likely a checkerboard even if it was a homogeneous one at n = nc. 

> IV. ANALYTIC CONSIDERATION

For simplicity of the analytic treatment, we assume that the system is spin polarized, and fermions with only one spin component undergo a transformation from the FL to a polaron state. For spinless fermions, there is no phonon-mediated pairing into singlet pairs, hence no bi-polarons. Also, for a parabolic dispersion, ŌČr =

ŌČ0(1 ‚ąí őĽ0)1/2 with no factor of 2 in front of őĽ0. Ex-tension to the spin-full fermions is straightforward, but requires a separate analysis. We further assume that the bare ŌČ0(q) = ŌČ0 is momentum independent (an Einstein phonon). Anticipating that the polaron physics involves energies of order W rather than of order EF , we intro-duce another coupling constant 

őĽp = g2

2ŌČ20 W (16) For an Einstein phonon, őĽ0 = 2 NF W őĽ p. The difference between őĽp and őĽ0 is most noticeable in small n. In three dimensions (3D), őĽ0 ‚ąĚ NF scales as n1/3, while őĽp

is independent of n. In 2D, őĽ0 remains finite at n ‚Üí 0, but still depends on the structure of fermionic excitations 13 near the bottom of the band, while őĽp depends on the bandwidth W . For comparison with the numerical re-sults from Sec. III we use the same tight-binding disper-sion ŌĶk = ‚ąí2t P2 

> őĪ=1

cos( kőĪa), with bandwidth W = 8 t

őĽp by changing the bandwidth W . We introduce

őĽp and a set of polaron őī-functional peaks at őĽp ‚Üí ‚ąě .Our goal is to understand how DOS evolves from one form to another and at which őĽp polaron peaks develop. For this purpose, it is instructive to first consider the limits n ‚Üí 0 and n ‚Üí 1 when only one set of őī-functions is present, either at ŌČ > 0 or ŌČ < 0, and then analyze an arbitrary 0 < n < 1 when the DOS in the Holstein model has őī‚ąífunctional peaks both positive and negative ŌČ.14  

> B. The limit of vanishing density

Before we proceed, a comment is in order. The small density limit should be understood either as the small, but still finite n, in which the Fermi energy EF ‚ąľ nW 

is much lower than W , but still higher than ŌČ0, i.e. 1 ‚Čę n ‚Čę ŌČ0/W (range A), or the range of the smallest 

n, where EF ‚Č™ ŌČ0 (range B). In range A, the Eliashberg parameter őĽE 

> 0

is still parametrically smaller than őĽ0, the dressed ŌČr (q = 0) scales as (1 ‚ąí 2őĽ0), and MET is rig-orously justified as long as 1 ‚ąí 2őĽ0 > (ŌČ0/E F )2 In range B, which includes n = 0, the adiabatic condition does not hold. We explicitly verified (see Appendix A) that in this range vertex corrections for low-energy fermions are controlled by the same őĽ0 as the mass renormalization, i.e. őĽE 

> 0

‚ąľ őĽ0 (In other words, the Eliashberg parameter is (roughly) ŌČ0/(EF + ŌČ0).) MET for low-energy excita-tions then holds up to őĽ0 = O(1), but there is no region where a strong coupling MET is under theoretical con-trol. We emphasize that in both region A and region B, the ratio ŌČ0/W is small. In this respect, our regime B is still different from a truly anti-adiabatic regime ŌČ0 > W .The numerical results for the smallest n have been ob-tained in range A, and in our analysis of the interplay between polaron formation and the internal stability of MET we will focus on 1 ‚Čę n ‚Čę ŌČ0/W restricting to this range would be prolematic if relevant changes in the spectral function at a finite W occurred at W ‚ąľ ŌČ0. We show, however, that the changes in the spectral function begin at much larger W ‚ąľ ‚ąöő≤ŌČ 0, when ŌČ0/W ‚ąľ 1/‚ąöő≤

and ŌČ0/E F ‚ąľ 1/(n‚ąöő≤). We can then set minimal n to be somewhat larger than 1 /‚ąöő≤ and treat it effectively as the limit n ‚Üí 0 as the corrections due to n are O(n) and for minimal n they are small in 1 /‚ąöő≤. 

> 1. Zero bandwidth, Holstein model

At W = 0, the limit n ‚Üí 0 can be taken by setting n =0 in the exact solution (24)-(26). The poles of GH (ŌČ, 0) are located at positive frequencies, and the smallest peak frequency is ŌČ = 0 (Fig. 7). To describe how this DOS evolves at a finite W , we need an analytic computational approach (a compliment to the diagrammatic Monte Carlo technique [28, 29]) which, on the one hand, captures polaron bound states at 

W = 0 and, on the other hand, can be extended to a finite 

W . We argue, following earlier works, e.g. Refs. [30, 31], that polaron bound states at ŌČ = nŌČ 0, n = 0 , 1, 2, . . . can be captured using diagrammatic expansion, which treats the renormalizations of the internal fermionic lines and vertex corrections on equal footing. The approach is of-ten termed ‚ÄĚeikonal‚ÄĚ, where the notation has been bor-rowed from scattering theory, where the diagrammatic treatment is similar [32]. More specifically, in the follow-ing, we call ‚ÄĚeikonal‚ÄĚ the computational method which

includes all diagrams linked to a single line and neglects diagrams with fermionic loops. We argue that the lat-ter vanish identically in the limits of zero and maximal fermionic density and also vanish at a finite density for a homogeneous arrangement of polarons. In Appendix C we compare the eikonal approach with two approximate calculations, both neglecting vertex corrections: the rain-bow approximation and the self-consistent one-loop ap-proximation. We show that the rainbow approximation fails to reproduce the salient features of the exact solu-tion of the Holstein model. The self-consistent one-loop approximation reproduces the discrete spectrum of the DOS but fails to reproduce the structure of the residues of the peaks, particularly at large ő≤.The eikonal computational approach has been used to treat the effects of scattering by static impurities [33‚Äď 37], by charge fluctuations in one-dimensional systems [38, 39] and near a nematic transition in 2D [40], and by spin fluctuations [41‚Äď47]. A straightforward analysis shows that at higher orders one has to include series of diagrams stringed to a single line, see (Fig. 8b). These diagrams contain vertex cor-rections and the corrections to internal fermionic prop-agators. There is no Migdal theorem for dispersion-less fermions, hence both corrections have to be treated on equal footing. Diagrams, which are not stringed to a sin-gle line, all vanish because they contain bubbles made of fermionic propagators with the poles in the same half-plane of frequency. For the same reason, the polarization operator that could potentially lead to renormalization of ŌČ0, also vanishes. Ge(kŌČ 0 + ňú ŌČ) = ( e‚ąíő≤ ő≤k/k !) /ňúŌČ, the same as GH (kŌČ 0 + ňú ŌČ, 0) [53] This calculation also clarifies how we should view a polaron within this approach. Like we said in the intro-duction, a polaron can generally be viewed as a ‚ÄĚbound state‚ÄĚ between a fermion and lattice distortion, i.e., be-tween a fermion and a phonon cloud. The issue is how many phonons are in the cloud. We argue that this num-ber is of order ő≤. Indeed, we found above that one needs 17          

> FIG. 10. Function Tm(ő≤) from Eq. (42) for m= 20 terms in the continued fractions expansion. Dashed line show the limiting behaviors for m > ő≤e (red) and m < ő≤e (blue); see text.

m ‚ąľ ő≤ terms in continued fractions to reproduce polaron peaks. Each subsequent term in fractions adds an addi-tional interaction with a phonon, so the m‚ąíth term can be viewed as the result of subsequent interactions with 

m phonons. Since relevant m are of order ő≤, the relevant number of phonons, which contribute to the formation of polarons, is of order ő≤ (more precisely, the number is close to ő≤e ). We note in passing that this is different from how a polaron is treated in Lang-Firsov approach [16, 25, 26]. There, a polaron is viewed as the result of a shift in the equilibrium position of a local oscillator in the presence of an electron. The Hamiltonian of a displaced oscillator re-duces to the sum of energies of a free dressed phonon and free electron, the latter with the energy shifted by ‚ąíő≤ŌČ 0.In these variables, a polaron is a free fermion without a cloud of dressed phonons. The equivalence between Lang-Firsov and our approach is established when one computes the fermionic Green‚Äôs function in Lang-Firsov approach by evaluating the overlap between the original and displaced phonon oscillator. In Fig. 11 we show the DOS obtained by taking 20 terms in continued fractions compared to the exact DOS 

‚ąí1/ŌÄ Im GH (ŌČ+i0, 0) where GH is given by (25). We see that for ő≤ ‚Č§ 1 the agreement is essentially perfect. For larger ő≤ > 20 /e ‚Čą 7.4, the agreement is poor, implying that more terms are needed in the continued fractions. We can go further and obtain the analytical expres-sion for the eikonal series for Ge(ŌČ) at any ŌČ. This is most straightforwardly done in the imaginary time rep-resentation. We verified that the exponentiation correctly accounts for higher-order diagrams, i.e. if we expand the exponent in Taylor series and convert each term back to momentum space, we reproduce order-by-order perturbation theory.

This leads to the DOS at small ŌČ, con-sisting of narrow patches, which remain well separated even at W > ŌČ 0, when naive reasoning would suggest overlapping of the DOS of neighboring excited polaron states. This also justifies a‚Äôposteriori our conjecture that at a non-zero W , őľ = ‚ąíő≤ŌČ 0 up to e‚ąíő≤ corrections. We recall that we neglected numerically small shifts of the chemical potential due to virtual delocaliza-tion of polaron states to the nearest-neighbor sites (they are quantified in Sect. IV D 3). Fermions at frequencies ŌČ ‚ąľ ő≤ŌČ 0 display different be-havior. Like we said, at W = 0, the DOS of these fermions can be well approximated by the Gaussian cen-tered at ŌČ = ő≤ŌČ 0 with the width ‚ąöő≤ŌČ 0 and can be fur-ther approximated by a single őī‚ąífunction at ŌČ = ő≤ŌČ 0

for frequencies |ŌČ ‚ąí ő≤ŌČ 0| larger than the width of the Gaussian, ‚ąöő≤ŌČ 0. We emphasize that this holds for the large ő≤ we consider here. For ő≤ = O(1) there is no clear separation between polaron peaks at different frequencies (see Appendix B). We emphasize that the transforma-tion of the DOS from its form in the atomic limit begins at W ‚ąľ ‚ąöő≤ŌČ 0 ‚Čę ŌČ0. There are no notable changes in DOS at W ‚ąľ ŌČ0.The approximation of states at ŌČ ‚ąľ ő≤ŌČ 0 by a single free-fermion peak becomes even better at a non-zero W .The residues of individual őī-functions with m ‚Čą ő≤ scale as Zm ‚ąľ 1/‚ąöő≤, i.e., individual peaks begin to overlap at W ‚ąľ ‚ąöő≤ŌČ 0. At larger W , individual peaks are no longer distinguishable, and also the bandwidth exceeds the width of the Gaussian made out of these states. As a consequence, the DOS near ŌČ = ő≤ŌČ 0 can be interpreted as that of a free dispersing fermion, described by a free-fermion Green‚Äôs function Ge

> 0

(k, ŌČ ), Eq. (52). This DOS is a continuum of width W . The full DOS then con-sists of this continuum and a set of narrow patches near 

ŌČ = 0, which are the DOS‚Äôs of weakly dispersing heavy polarons. We show this DOS in Fig. 13a. In Appendix E we discuss in more detail how individual peaks near 

ŌČ = ő≤ŌČ 0 transform into a continuum when W ‚ąľ ‚ąöő≤ŌČ 0.As W increases, the lower end of the continuum ex-tends to smaller ŌČ. In this process, it absorbs polaron patches one by one, starting from one ones closest to the continuum. We show this in Fig. 13b. At ő≤ŌČ 0 = W/ 2, i.e., at őĽp = 1 /2, the continuum absorbs the last polaron at ŌČ = 0 (Fig. 13c). This is the end point of the po-laron state. At larger W , the system is in the FL phase and the DOS N (ŌČ) is continuous between ŌČ = 0 and 

ŌČ = W . That critical őĽp = 1 /2 is corroborated by the observation that for this őĽp, the chemical potential of the polaron state őľ = ‚ąíő≤ŌČ 0 coincides with the chemi-20

However, as we said in Sec. III, the difference between the kinetic energies Ekin ,F L and Ekin ,F G and between őľF G and őľF L ) is small in the Eliashberg pa-rameter, which we treat as infinitesimally small. For this reason, in the following we approximate őľF L by őľF G and 

Ekin ,F L by Ekin ,F G . Second, in principle, there exist cor-rections to the chemical potential of the polaron state

The absorption of polarons with energies of order ŌČ0 the growing continuum can be equiv-alently described by the growth of the spectral weight in between polaron patches. We don‚Äôt have rigorous de-scription for this, but we emphasize that the logics be-hind exponentially small ( eő≤ ) width of the polaron peak is that the factor eő≤ comes from continued fractions of order m ‚ąľ ő≤, when the relevant phonon frequency is comparable to ő≤ŌČ 0. At W parametrically smaller than 

ő≤ŌČ , the corrections from the fermionic dispersion to con-tinued fraction result at this order are small and can be neglcted. Howeverer, at W ‚ąľ ő≤ŌČ 0, they become relevant at eventually destroy polaron patches. It is also instructive to discuss the evolution of the sys-tem behavior starting from the opposite limit of small őĽp

(large W ), where MET is valid. We recall that MET is assumed to remain internally stable as long as the dressed phonon Debye frequency ŌČr is positive [5‚Äď7, 55] (barring potential dynamical instabilities at smaller őĽp [13]). As we said above, in our model ŌČr remains positive up to 

őĽ0 = 1. In terms of őĽp = ŌÄőĽ 0/4, the stability holds up to őĽp = ŌÄ/ 4. This coupling is larger than 1 /2, mean-ing that there is a range of őĽp where the FL state is a local minimum with respect to low-energy perturbations within MET, yet the polaron state has a lower energy. This last statement may sound contradictory because Fig. 13, viewed from right to left, shows that the po-laron bound state develops at ŌČ = 0, which at a face value looks like a low-energy instability. However, we ar-gue that polaron formation is a high-energy phenomenon. This becomes clear from the analysis of the fermionic self-energy. It has two contributions. One comes from low loop-orders in perturbation theory ( m = O(1), where m

is a loop order) and involves internal fermions with fre-quencies well within the bandwidth. This contribution is captured within MET. It becomes singular when the dressed phonon softens, but is regular at smaller őĽp, in-cluding őĽp = 1 /2. Another comes from high-loop orders 

m ‚Č• W/ŌČ 0, from the processes in which multiple phonon scattering moves an internal fermion from small ŌČ to out-side of the bandwidth. The contribution to self-energy from these processes is of the order ( őĽp)W/ŌČ 0 . When őĽp is small, the corresponding self-energy is irrelevant. How-ever, when őĽp > 1, it becomes exponentially large and 21 causes a dip in N (ŌČ) at ŌČ = 0, which is the beginning of the formation of the polaron state. A more sophisticated analysis is needed to verify that this occurs at őĽp = 1 /2. We also note that the Debye frequency changes discontinuously at őĽp = 1 /2 from ŌČr (q) in MET to ŌČ0 in the polaron state. However, at n = 0 +, this discontinuity affects only infinitesimally small q as ŌČr in a 2D FL gets reduced with increasing őĽp only for q < 2kF , where 

kF ‚ąĚ n1/2, while at larger q, ŌČr (q) ‚Čą ŌČ0.

> D. Arbitrary filling, 0< n < 1
> 1. Zero bandwidth, Holstein model

The exact spectral function of the Holstein model 

AH (ŌČ, n ) at 0 < n < 1 is presented in Eq. (27). It consists of a set of őī‚ąífunctions at both positive and neg-ative ŌČn = nŌČ 0, n = 0 , ¬Ī1, ¬Ī2, etc. The total spectral weight at positive frequencies is 1 ‚ąí n and that at neg-ative frequencies is n. We argued earlier that at large 

|ŌČ| ‚Čą ő≤ŌČ 0, where the distance between the peaks is much smaller than their positions, the spectral function can be approximated by a Gaussian envelope. For 0 < n < 1, there are two envelopes, one centered at ŌČ = ő≤ŌČ 0 and the other at ŌČ = ‚ąíő≤ŌČ 0. Each envelope has a small width ‚ąöő≤ŌČ 0 ‚Č™ ő≤ŌČ 0 and can be further approximated by a őī-function at ŌČ = ¬Īő≤ŌČ 0 with residue Z = 1 ‚ąín for negative 

ŌČ and Z = n for positive ŌČ:

A(ŌČ, n ) = nőī (ŌČ + ő≤ŌČ 0) + (1 ‚ąí n)őī(ŌČ ‚ąí ő≤ŌČ 0) . (58) The corresponding ‚ÄĚfree-fermion‚ÄĚ retarded Green‚Äôs func-tion is 

Gret (ŌČ, n ) = nŌČ + ő≤ŌČ 0 + iőī + 1 ‚ąí nŌČ ‚ąí ő≤ŌČ 0 + iőī (59) The two-peak structure in (58) is qualitatively different from the one-peak structure of A(ŌČ) at n = 0 and n =1. There, the free-fermion part of the Green‚Äôs function coincides with the bare Ge

> 0

(ŌČ) in the eikonal approach. This is clearly not the case at a finite n as starting from a Green‚Äôs function with a single pole one has to include the self-energy to reproduce the two-pole structure of G(ŌČ, n )in (59). A self-energy of this form emerges if we assume that there exists another branch of excitations with opposite sign of őľn (an ancilla fermion) and that there is a bilin-ear coupling between the physical and ancilla fermions. A somewhat similar approach has been used in the anal-ysis of pseudogap behavior for hole doped cuprates (see Ref. [56] for a recent review). In our case, the physical reasoning for two-fermion description is that at 0 < n < 1each lattice site is either occupied or empty with a cer-tain probability. In this respect, a physical fermion de-scribes states occupied with probability n and an an-cilla fermion describes states occupied with probability 23 1 ‚ąí n. n = 1. Using the results of the previous two Sections, we then find the DOS consisting of two independent pieces, one at positive and one at negative ŌČ. Each DOS is a combination of a free-particle continuum with width W ,centered at ŌČ = ¬Īő≤ŌČ 0, and exponentially narrow patches of polaron DOS, centered at ŌČ = ¬ĪnŌČ 0 (Fig. 17 a). As W increases ( őĽp decreases), the two continua become wider and their lower ends move to smaller ŌČ absorbing polaron peaks one by one (Fig. 17 b). The last polaron gets absorbed at őĽp = 1 /2. At this őĽp, the DOS consists of two continua touching each other at ŌČ = 0 (Fig. 17 c). We emphasize that this DOS is still very different from that of the FL. Namely, the DOS has two peaks (two van Hove singularities), and the total width of the range where it is non-zero is 2 W as opposed to W in a FL. The DOS also evolves with őĽp. At őĽp ‚Č§ 1/2, it dis-plays two peaks at ŌČ = ¬ĪE and is non-zero between the peaks (see Fig. 19). The profile of the DOS evolves due to the evolution of E and of the coherence factors (1 /2)(1 ¬Ī őľn/pőľn2 + |‚ąÜ0|2), but as long as ‚ąÜ 0 is non-zero, N (ŌČ) has two peaks (van Hove singularities) at fi-nite frequencies ŌČ = ¬ĪE and is non-zero between the peaks. The structure of this DOS is similar to that in the pseudogap (PG) phase in the cuprates, and by anal-ogy we label this intermediate state as the PG state. It does not possess a set of polaron patches, which are absorbed by the two continua, but is still qualitatively different from the DOS in a FL. Finally, at őĽp = őĽc, 1 

> p

,the residue of the two peaks in the DOS vanishes, and the DOS becomes the same as in a FL. At this coupling, the chemical potential őľn coincides with őľF L ‚Čą őľF G ,introduced in (99), (100). At smaller őĽp, |‚ąÜ0| = 0, the ancilla fermion does not play a role, and the system is in the FL state, described by MET. Luttinger theorem and zeros of the Green‚Äôs function 

In an FL, the area of an electron Fermi surface, SF S ,is related to the fermionic density by the Luttinger the-orem. In our case of spinless fermions, the relation is simply SF S = n. In the mixed state (or equivalently, the pseudogap state), the density of the Fermi liquid com-ponent changes to őī < n . In this situation, we expect that the conventional relation becomes invalid and the modified one becomes 

SF S = őī, (121) where őī is given by (115). We now derive this expression staring from the relation between the density and the frequency integral of the Green‚Äôs function Gc(ŌĶ, ŌČ )

n1 = n ‚ąí őī moves into a polaron state without a Fermi surface. In this respect, there is a certain similarity be-tween our mixed phase and FL ‚ąó phase proposed in spin-liquid (fractionalized FL) theory for cuprates and other strongly correlated materials [56, 59, 60]. In both cases, strong interactions transform an ordinary FL into a new state, which still has coherent FL quasiparticles (conduc-tion electron), but with a smaller FS, along with localized excitations without a Fermi surface. These localized ex-citations are polarons in our case and a spin liquid of local moments in FL ‚ąó.We also note that the Green‚Äôs function of a physical fermion in the mixed state has both poles and zeros. Interplay with CDW electronic order. 

We now argue that the phase diagram in Fig. 21 is valid for n < n c, where nc is some density smaller than 1/2, while at larger n there appear new phases in which an electronic state has a CDW order. The reasoning for a CDW-ordered electronic state comes from the compar-ison of the location of a critical line őĽc, 1 

> p

, above which a FL state described by MET becomes unstable towards polarons, and őĽc2 

> p

, above which a FL becomes unstable towards a CDW electronic order. We consider the struc-ture and energy of the electron states with a non-zero CDW order later in Sec. IV D 4 and here identify őĽp for the onset of a CDW order. The CDW instability develops when the dressed phonon frequency vanishes at some q; in our analytical model of q‚ąíindependent bare ŌČ0 and spin-less fermions, this happens when 2 őĽpW ő†st (q) = 1, (see Eq. (6)), where the static polarization bubble does not have a spin fac-tor of 2. At small n, we found earlier that őĽc, 1 

> p

‚Č§ 1/2is smaller than őĽc2 

> n

‚Čą ŌÄ/ 4, i.e. the polaron state devel-ops before the FL state becomes unstable towards CDW. However, the situation is different near half-filling. Here, the polarization bubble is the largest for q ‚Čą Q = ( ŌÄ, ŌÄ )as ő† st (Q) diverges as (1 /W )(log |1/2 ‚ąí n|)2. Then őĽc2

> p

disappears as 1 /(log |1/2 ‚ąí n|)2. The other critical cou-pling őĽc, 1 

> p

also goes to zero in the approach to half-filling but only as 1 /(log |1/2 ‚ąí n|). As a result, near n = 1 /2, 

őĽc2 

> p

< őĽ c, 1 

> p

, which implies that MET becomes unstable to-wards CDW before the polaron state develops. The com-plete analysis of the density dependence of őĽc2 

> p

is some-what complicated because the momentum q, at which the dressed Debye frequency softens, also depends on n. At 32 small n, the leading instability is at q = ( qc, 0) or (0 , q c), where qc increases with n. At n = n0 ‚Čą 0.18, qc reaches 

ŌÄ, and at larger n the momentum of the CDW instabil-ity is q = ( ŌÄ, q c) or qc, ŌÄ ). At n ‚Üí 1/2, qc approaches 

ŌÄ and the CDW order develops with momentum Q. We show the density variation of the CDW momentum q in Fig. 22). In Fig. 23a we plot őĽc2 

> p

as a function of n, which we obtained using Fig. 22) as input. In Fig. 23b we plot both őĽc, 1 

> p

and őĽc2 

> p

őĽc2

< őĽ c, 1 

> p

, i.e., the CDW order develops before the order parameter ‚ąÜ 0 becomes non-zero. This observation poses a question of how the critical line for the onset of a CDW order evolves within the mixed state, where the electronic density őī varies between 0 and n (see Eq. (117) and discussion around it). We call the value of the electron density, above which the CDW order develops inside the mixed state őīc because őī

depends on őĽp but not on n, see Eqs. (111) and (113), 

őīc also does not depend on n and for this reason is the same as nc. In terms of number, we find őīc = nc ‚Čą 0.17. The corresponding őĽp ‚Čą 0.4. At n > n c, there are two critical lines for the electronic CDW order: the lower one is őĽc, 2 

> p

> p

(n) < őĽ < őĽ c, 1

őĽp < 1/2 as just the pseudogap phase, as we did in the first part of Sec. IV D 2. Indeed, in this description, the phonon frequency ŌČ0 is renormalized into ŌČr (q) due to contributions from particle-hole bubbles made of őĪ

őĽp < 1/2. The dressed phonon frequency then softens at 

őĽp = 0 .4. In the left panel of Fig. 2 we present the analytical phase diagram which contains the homogeneous polaron state, the FL state, the CDW state and the mixed phase split into two parts, in one of which the electronic com-ponent is CDW-ordered.  

> 3. CDW polaron order

In the analysis earlier in this Section we assumed that the polaron condensate at 0 < n < 1 is a homoge-neous one. We now analyze a potential emergence of a CDW-type polaron state in which the order parameter ‚ąÜ( q) has a finite momentum q. Such a state emerges if its energy is smaller than that of the homogeneous po-laron state. The ground state energies of the polaron states with different q may differ for two reasons. First, there is a q-dependent difference in the kinetic energy of polarons, which can move throughout the lattice co-herently by simultaneously rearranging the oscillator dis-placements. This kinetic energy is exponentially small, of order ‚ąľ W e ‚ąíő≤ , yet it may overcome an effective repulsion between fermions and at low density favors a homoge-neous q = 0 order for polarons made of spinless fermions and the BEC state of bi-polarons for spin-full fermions. Second, there is an energy variation with q due to virtual fermion delocalization relative to the strong oscillator dis-placement. In leading order in W 2, it comes from the hopping of fermions to the nearest-neighbor sites without 

rearranging the phonon displacement field. At large őĽp

this energy variation can be studied perturbatively start-ing from a localized polaron state, i.e., the one with a flat ‚ąÜq. A fermion can fluctuate to the nearest-neighbor site with a matrix element t by leaving behind a large oscil-lator displacement. In the virtual state, the energy in-creases by 2 ő≤ŌČ 0 (+ ő≤ŌČ 0 compared to the original ‚ąíő≤ŌČ 0)Assuming that all nearest-neighbor sites on the square lattice are not occupied, the second-order correction to the energy of a localized polaron due to these processes is

> 4. Electronic CDW order with a finite order parameter

The phase diagram includes a pure FL state, a pure checkerboard polaron state (polaron CDW), a CDW state, and two mixed states: MS 2 (FL and polaron CDW) and MS 3 (CDW and polaron CDW). The lines approaching n = 1 /2 should be viewed as describing system behavior at densities arbitrary close but not exactly equal to 1/2. For n ‚Č° 1/2, the behavior is special because of degener-acy between an electronic and polaronic CDW.

> 5. Degeneracy at half-filling

Comparing the self-consistent equations and the ex-pressions for the ground state energy for the electronic and polaronic ( ŌÄ, ŌÄ ) order parameters at n = 1 /2, Eqs. (167) and (148) and Eqs. (166) and (142), respectively, we see that the two sets of equations are identical. The dressed electron-phonon interactions, Eqs. (161) and (58), are also identical because the coherence factors uk

and vk have the same form in the two cases at őľn = 0. The equivalence implies that at half-filling there is a de-generacy between the checkerboard electron and polaron orders. To analyze this degeneracy in more detail, we introduce ancilla fermions and keep the two terms in the effective phonon-mediated 4-fermion interaction Uef f : the one be-tween the densities of the physical c‚ąí fermions and the other between the densities of the physical and ancilla fermions. We decouple Uef f by introducing two order parameters: an electronic checkerboard with q = Q and a polaron checkerboard with the same q = Q. The elec-tronic checkerboard order parameter ‚ąÜ el Q is real, but the polaron checkerboard order parameter ‚ąÜ Q, which we call in this section ‚ąÜ pQ, is generally complex: ‚ąÜ pQ = |‚ąÜpQ|eiŌē .Diagonalizing the effective 4 √ó 4 quadratic Hamiltonian, we find that in the ground state, ‚ąÜ pQ is purely imagi-nary (i.e., ‚ÄĚorthogonal‚ÄĚ to real ‚ąÜ el Q). The ground state is an insulator with two doubly degenerate bands, whose energy Ek = ¬ĪpŌĶ2

> V. COMPARISON BETWEEN NUMERICAL AND ANALYTIC RESULTS AND THE FULL PHASE DIAGRAM

We begin with several observations. First, in the an-alytical study we considered the 2D case and assumed that the bare ŌČ0 is independent of q. In the numeri-cal study, we considered several forms of ŌČ0(q) and both 2D and 3D systems. For comparison between analyt-ical and numerical results, we select the lower panel of Fig. 5 which is for the same 2D case with q‚ąíindependent 

ŌČ0. Second, the numerical results in Fig. 5 are pre-sented in units of őĽ0 = NF g2/ŌČ 20 , which measures the strength of interaction near the Fermi surface in MET (see (2)), while the analytical results are presented in terms of őĽp = g2/(2 ŌČ20 W ), which measures coupling to fermions with energies comparable to the bandwidth. Third, the numerical results have been obtained for spin-1/2 fermions, while the analytical results are for spin-less fermions. To move from S = 1 /2 to spin-less fermions, one has to re-scale the density and the electron polariza-tion by a factor of two. With this rescaling included, the relation between őĽ0 and őĽp is 

őĽ0 = őĽp (NF W ) (174) For our tight-binding model, NF = N (őľF L ) =(4 /ŌÄ 2W )K(1 ‚ąí ňÜőľ2

> F L

), where ňÜ őľF L = 2 őľF L /W is related to the density n by Eq. (100). At small n, ňÜ őľF L ‚Üí ‚ąí 1 and 

NF ‚Čą 2/(ŌÄW ); at n ‚Üí 1/2, ňÜ őľF L ‚Üí 0, and NF diverges logarithmically. To make the comparison between analytical and nu-merical results more straightforward, in Fig. 2, which we presented at the beginning of this paper, we plot the nu-merical phase diagram in 2D in units of őĽp, adjusted to spin-less fermions, along with the analytical phase dia-gram for the case of a homogeneous order of polarons with ‚ąÜ( q) = ‚ąÜ( q = 0). Comparing the two phase dia-grams, we see that they are essentially identical. This is not surprising because in the numerical study we iden-tified a homogeneous polaron state as a localized one, with no fluctuations between the sites occupied by po-larons and empty sites. In the analytical study, we used probabilistic description and expressed Green‚Äôs function at a given site (the spatial Fourier transform of Gc(ŌČ, ŌĶ k)) as the sum of the Green‚Äôs functions of the operators őĪ

and ňú őĪ, weighted with the factors 1 ‚ąí n and n, respec-tively. Operators őĪ and ňú őĪ describe unoccupied states with ni = 0 and occupied states with ni = 1. There is no phonon assisted hopping between unoccupied and occupied sites even when W is finite; hence this polaron state is fully localized. We emphasize that while the phase digrams for spin-full and spin-less fermions are identical, the DOS are not. Already in the atomic limit, the DOS for the spin-full case contains a true gap around ŌČ = 0 associated with the fi-nite minimal energy of a bi-polaron, while the DOS in the spin-less case contains a set of polaron őī‚ąífunctional peaks down to ŌČ = 0. The evolution of the DOS with increasing W is the same for the two cases, if we restrict with the continuum of states at ŌČ ‚ąľ ¬Ī ő≤ŌČ 0, but beyond this approximation, there are qualitative distinctions be-tween spin-full and spin-less fermions. Namely, for bi-polarons, the true gap in the DOS still holds at at a small but finite W , i.e. the system of S = 1 /2 fermions remains an insulator. The two boundaries of the mixed state are then the actual phase transition lines: the one at a larger 

őĽ0 is an insulator to a metal transition, and the lower one is a transition from a metal with broken Luttinger theo-rem to a conventional metal in which Luttinger theorem holds. For spin-less fermions, at W > 0, the sub-gaps between polaron patches hold within our approximation, but beyond it, there is an exponentially small damping rate for a decay of states with a finite ŌČ (see Appendix E for more discussion on this). As a consequence, the DOS in between polaron patches is exponentially small but still finite. Then, strictly speaking, the system is a metal at any finite W . From this perspective, the upper boundary of the mixed phase is a very sharp crossover but not a true phase transition. The lower boundary of the mixed phase is a true phase transition for the same reason as for spin-full fermions ‚Äď the Luttinger theorem gets broken. The numerical and analytical phase diagrams for the checkerboard polaron state are shown in Fig. 27. The analytical phase diagram is a suggested one, as we dis-cussed in Sec. IV D 3. We emphasize that the checker-board states in the numerical and analytical studies were treated differently. For the numerical study, we selected a localized state with strict checkerboard order of po-larons in a cluster ( ni = 1 at even sites inside the cluster and ni = 0 at odd sites and vise versa) and no polarons outside a cluster. For Einstein phonon this state is ener-getically degenerate with any other configuration of po-larons, and only gains extra energy if we include virtual fluctuations to the n.n. sites. In the analytical study, we set ‚ąÜ( q) = ‚ąÜ( q = Q), used probabilistic description and expressed the Green‚Äôs function of a physical fermion via the Green‚Äôs function of őĪ and ňú őĪ fermions, which de-scribe filled and empty polaron states at a given site. The probability to be either in őĪ or ňú őĪ state depends on 

ŌĶk; in the real space, the probabilities vary between even and odd sites. This state has some similarities with the (1 ‚ąí 0)-type polaron state used in the numerical study; however, the variation of probabilities is weak at large őĽp.In addition, the state with ‚ąÜ( q) = ‚ąÜ( Q) is not localized as H‚Ä≤ 

> e‚ąíph

generates phonon-assisted hopping between the occupied and empty sites. Nevertheless, a similarity be-tween the numerical and analytic phase diagrams shows that both approaches capture the same physics. We emphasize that the phase diagrams that we presented, both for homogeneous and (ŌÄ, pi ) po-laron/bi=polaron orders, hold for large ő≤. For small ő≤,41 the transformation for the atomic limit to MET at large 

W is different (see, e.g., [68]). The key reason for the dif-ference is that polarons-bi-polarons cannot be viewed as bound states of a fermion and a large number of phonons attracted to it.  

> A. The full phase diagram

For the full phase diagram, we assume that the po-laron order is homogeneous for n away from half-filling and checkerboard near half-filling. We assume that the phase diagrams are similar for both types of polaron or-der and contain the mixed phase, which in some range of densities near half-filling is split into the regions where the electronic component is in a FL state and where it has a CDW order. We show the candidate phase dia-gram in Fig. 3. In the doping range where the polaron order is homogeneous, the phase boundaries can be de-termined by exact calculations. For the checkerboard polaron order, the phase boundaries are drawn by hand. At n = 1 /2, the states with ( ŌÄ, ŌÄ ) polaron and electron order are degenerate.  

> B. Comparison with other works

Properties of e-ph systems at strong-coupling, and the associated tendencies toward polaron/bi-polaron, have been extensively studied numerically using Monte Carlo simulation [69‚Äď72] and dynamical mean-field the-ory (DMFT) methods [49, 68, 73‚Äď80]. In most of these studies, the primary focus was the influence of bi-polaron formation for spin-full fermions on superconductivity and of polarons/bi-polarons on the normal state transport at nonzero temperatures. In our study, we restricted ourselves to T = 0, neglected the potential supercon-ductivity in the variational analysis, and performed an-alytical calculations for spin-less fermions. Some of the previous work also focused on CDW instabilities. The authors of [70‚Äď72, 76] found that in systems near half-filling (and, in general, away from perfect Fermi sur-face nesting), strong electron-phonon coupling leads to commensurate ( ŌÄ, ŌÄ ) charge-density wave ground states At dilute concentrations, incommensurate charge-density waves [76] and phase separation [72] have been reported. These findings are generally consistent with our analysis. A transformation from a FL to polaron (or bi-polaron) regime was analyzed in [68, 70, 72, 74, 75, 78, 79, 81], with connections drawn to high-temperature superconductiv-ity [81] and the metal-insulator transition [68, 78, 79]. In some of these works [72‚Äď75, 79] the formation of polarons / bi-polarons was described in terms of bimodal distribu-tion of phonon displacements, interpreted [74, 75] as the appearance of frozen-in lattice distortions. This scenario is qualitatively and in several aspects also quantitatively similar to our ‚Äúancilla fermion‚ÄĚ scenario for the homoge-neous polaron state. To be more precise here, we compare our results with those of Ref. [74, 75] by Millis, Mueller, and Shraiman (MMS). They considered FL to polaron crossover within DMFT for several models, including the one for spin-less fermions with a semi-circular DOS and a dispersionles boson, which is most directly related to our model. MMS focused on the limit where (in our notation) ŌČ0 ‚Üí 0while ő≤ŌČ 0 remains finite (i.e., ő≤ tends to infinity). In this limit, a phonon propagator reduces to őī(ő©), i.e., a phonon can be treated classically. Because ŌČ0 = 0+, there are no separate polaron states at discrete ŌČ = mŌČ 0 in the atomic limit, őĽp = ‚ąě. Yet, the minimization of energy within the DMFT yields frozen-in lattice distortions of opposite sign on occupied and unoccupied sites, which gives rise to two őī‚ąífunctional peaks in the DOS at ¬Īő≤ŌČ 0,one with residue n, and another with residue 1 ‚ąí n. This fully agrees with our result at ő≤ ‚Üí ‚ąě (and also with the exact solution of a single-site Holsten model at near-infinite ő≤). At large but finite őĽp, MMS found the two-patch form of the DOS N (ŌČ), one patch at positive and another at negative ŌČ. In between, N (ŌČ) = 0. This again agrees with our result modulo that our DOS has polaron peaks at smaller |ŌČ|. Finally, MMS found an intermediate state in the range of őĽp, where frozen-in lattice distortions are still non-zero, yet N (ŌČ) is non-zero for all ŌČ and eventually becomes the same as in a FL when frozen-in lattice distortions disappear. This intermediate state is very similar to our psedogap/mixed state, where our order parameter ‚ąÜ 0 is non-zero, yet N (ŌČ) is non-zero for all ŌČ.For a direct comparison with MMS, we compute the local Green‚Äôs function and the DOS in our model, using a semi-circular form of the DOS for free fermions instead of (23):

Their results for spinless fermions can be directly compared to ours at n = 0, where a CDW instability does not interfere with polaron formation. Here, CEA found a cascade of transformations of the fermionic DOS upon decreasing 

őĽp, with the number of gapped regionsin the DOS be-43 ing reduces by one in each transformation. This is in full agreement with our evolution of the DOS, in which a growing continuum in the DOS upon decreasing őĽp ab-sorbs polaron patches one by one. Their evolution of the DOS within the polaron phase (e.g., Fig. 12 from [49]) is also very similar to ours at W ‚Č• ‚ąöő≤ŌČ 0 (see Appendix E). The only difference is that CEA consider the continuum as incoherent, while we associate the continuum with a free-fermion band. CEA also argued that the number of phonons in the polaron state at the lowest ŌČ is of order ő≤.This fully agrees with our analysis of the structure of the continued fraction representation of the Green‚Äôs function in Sec. IV B 1. For half-filling, their and our results agree once we ex-tend our analysis to a semi-circular DOS, as described earlier in this Section, and neglect potential development of CDW order. One particular point of agreement here is the DMFT result [68, 78] that the DOS for spinless fermions remains finite at ŌČ = 0 for any value of őĽp, as long as ŌČ0 is finite. This agrees with our result that the zero-frequency polaron peak from the atomic limit trans-forms at finite W into a patch of exponentially small, but still finite, width of order ‚ąľ e‚ąíő≤ , and this patch eventu-ally merges with the continua. Their mapping of a po-laron state into a two-level system has some similarity with the introduction of an ancilla fermion in our theory. In the diagrammatic approach, a fermionic Green‚Äôs function at n = 0+ and finite W has also been ana-lyzed in Ref. [52] in the approximation in which ev-ery diagram for the self-energy is averaged over momen-tum. This yields the spectral function with an exponen-tially small width ( e‚ąíő≤ ) of all polaron peaks, including those at ŌČ ‚Čą ő≤ŌČ 0. In our view, this form is valid for 

ő≤ = O(1), when the residues of polaron peaks at ŌČ = 0 and ŌČ = ő≤ŌČ 0 are comparable. However, for large ő≤,we argued in this work that exponentially narrow po-laron patches hold only for ŌČ ‚ąľ ŌČ0, while fermions with 

ŌČ ‚Čą ő≤ŌČ 0 form a free-particle continuum, whose width is set by W for W > ŌČ 0

‚ąöő≤, and the evolution of the DOS at larger W ‚ąľ ő≤ŌČ 0 can be viewed as gradual absorption of polaron peaks by the continuum.   

> C. Additional considerations
> 1. 3D case

The 3D phase diagram, obtained in the variational study for dispersion-less ŌČ0 and spin-full fermions, is pre-sented in the middle of the lower panel in Fig. 4. For convenience, in Fig.31 we re-plot this phase diagram in units of őĽp and for spin-less fermions. We note that phase diagrams in 2D and 3D are similar, but there is one key distinction: in 3D the DOS of the FL vanishes as n1/3 at small n. As a consequence, MET remains stable against low-energy fluctuations up to őĽc, 2 

> p

(n) ‚ąĚ 1/N F ‚ąĚ 1/n 1/3.In the same limit, the homogeneous state of polarions emerges at őĽc, 1 

> p

‚Čą 1/2. This implies that at small n, the instability towards the polaron state occurs already at weak MET coupling, when the dressed phonon frequency is almost the same as ŌČ0.For larger n, the phase diagram is similar to that in 2D: there again exists an intermediate mixed phase between 

őĽp = 1 /2 and őĽc, 1 

> p

, where a portion of a system is at the end point of the homogeneous polaron state and another portion in the FL state. The line őĽc2 

> p

again lies below őĽc, 1

> p

at n > n c ‚Čą 0.2, and for these n there exists the CDW electronic order, sandwiched between őĽc, 2

őĽc, 2
